  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7e7775b8-03d4-406e-8045-d2f148c2f5fd'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer11606442433600194455">Eight-year-old Kahu, a member of the Maori tribe of Whangara, New Zealand, fights to prove her love, her leadership, and her destiny. Her people claim descent from Kahutia Te Rangi, the legendary ‘whale rider.’ In every generation since Kahutia, a male heir has inherited the title of chief. But now there is no male heir, and the aging chief is desperate to find a successor</span>
  <span id="freeText11606442433600194455" style="display:none">Eight-year-old Kahu, a member of the Maori tribe of Whangara, New Zealand, fights to prove her love, her leadership, and her destiny. Her people claim descent from Kahutia Te Rangi, the legendary ‘whale rider.’ In every generation since Kahutia, a male heir has inherited the title of chief. But now there is no male heir, and the aging chief is desperate to find a successor. Kahu is his only great-grandchild—and Maori tradition has no use for a girl. But when hundreds of whales beach themselves and threaten the future of the Maori tribe, Kahu will do anything to save them—even the impossible.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/994255-for-those-gr-members-who-live-in-nz-or">For Those GR members who Live in NZ or Spent Years in NZ:
How does this novel fit into reality in NZ? Is it total fantasy or is there a people waiting for their leader to make himself/herself known?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_994255'><a id="like_count_community_question_994255" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/994255?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F133497.The_Whale_Rider">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/30838991-samatha-lepaio"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1501400669i/30838991._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/30838991-samatha-lepaio">Samatha Lepaio</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The myth is very well-known as most people know of the ancestor who rode the ancient whale. Fitting into the reality of New Zealand? The idea of the w<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The myth is very well-known as most people know of the ancestor who rode the ancient whale. Fitting into the reality of New Zealand? The idea of the whale rider is a Maori myth but myths and legends are a huge part of any culture, and Maori's are very proud of theirs. But Kahu trying to prove to her Koro that she can be a leader even if she is a female is a strong representation of what this book is about.<br /><br />From someone who spent most of her life in New Zealand.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think the reading level would be advanced for a child that age, and also there are definitely scenes that would be upsetting and scary for elementar<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think the reading level would be advanced for a child that age, and also there are definitely scenes that would be upsetting and scary for elementary-school age kids. I would save it for junior high age and up, and even as an adult reader, I found parts of it pretty intense. Amazing story, though, and worth the read. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2167882720" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2167882720" />
    <a title="Brina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2933855-brina"><img alt="Brina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601675085p2/2933855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2167882720?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brina" href="/user/show/2933855-brina">Brina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=new-zealand">new-zealand</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2167882720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4183243073217544756">I read Whale Rider not even three years ago and fell in love with this tale. I got this book for my youngest daughter to read but she wasn’t interested, at least not yet, and I could not resist a reread. As my lead in to International Women’s Month, I returned to the story of Kahu of Whengara, New Zealand. <br/><br/>I have been fascinated by whales from the time I was a young child and saw a blue whale skeleton at the Chicago Field Museum of Natural History. This one event precipitated a lifelong love of </span>
  <span id="freeText4183243073217544756" style="display:none">I read Whale Rider not even three years ago and fell in love with this tale. I got this book for my youngest daughter to read but she wasn’t interested, at least not yet, and I could not resist a reread. As my lead in to International Women’s Month, I returned to the story of Kahu of Whengara, New Zealand. <br /><br />I have been fascinated by whales from the time I was a young child and saw a blue whale skeleton at the Chicago Field Museum of Natural History. This one event precipitated a lifelong love of whales and dolphins and all marine mammal life. I have been fortunate to go on two whale watches in my life but I have never gotten up close to these majestic creatures. With the year winding down and finding myself in need of an author whose last name starts with the letter I to finish an A-Z author challenge, I recently came across the novella Whale Rider by Maori writer Witi Ihimaera. Gaining international acclaim from the movie based on this book, Ihimaera takes his readers on a mythical journey through contemporary Maori culture.<br /><br />The Maori people originally came from the sea. The ancestor of the current people named Kahutia Te Rangi was able to converse with whales and the two species maintained a symbiotic relationship that balanced all creatures of the earth. Legend has it that an ancient whale named Paikea launched spears from the sea that landed all over the world, and these were responsible for the creation of the birds, animals, and ancient Maori people. The current Maori lead by Koro Apirana and his grandson Porourangi still hold by these ancient traditions and believe that in the current climate with whalers killing the kings of the ocean for sport, the balance holding the future of the earth together is doomed. They seek a leader for the next generation of their people, a male heir who is the reincarnation of the original whale rider Kahutia Te Rangi, who is able to converse with the gentle giants of the sea and restore balance to the earth.<br /><br />There may be a leader right before their eyes although Koro Apirana holds strongly to his traditions and does not realize that the future may hinge on his great granddaughter, Porourangi's daughter Kahu, named for the tribe's ancestor Kahutia Te Rangi who could speak to whales. While Koro believes that only a male heir can save his people, his wife Nanny Flowers attempts to foster a loving relationship between Kahu and her Paka (grandfather). A strong willed woman who is descended from a female dominated tribe, Nanny Flowers believes that women can do anything that a man can and more so if given the chance. Both Nanny Flowers and Rawiri, Porourangi's brother, witness how special Kahu may be from an early age, yet their attempts to get Koro Apirana to acknowledge this are fruitless. As a result, the chieftain conducts a tribal wide search to find a boy who will lead future generations of Maori people.<br /><br />Ihimaera notes that he wrote this book for his two daughters who one day asked him why only boys play the role of heroes in movies whereas girls are cast as the role of damsel in distress. He was living in New York at the time, and this traditional tale came to mind when a whale was stranded in the Hudson River and needed to be rescued. The character Kahutia was thus born. Kahu as an eight year old realizes that her people are suffering and is determined to become well versed in her culture, cultivating a one-sided loving relationship with Koro Apirana, and winning countless awards at her cultural school. More importantly, she can talk to whales and dolphins, if only her Paka Koro would see this. Kahu's role in saving the Maori comes to a head with the appearance of an ancient whale on the Whengara beach who is said to be Paikea, and only a true whale rider is able to save both the whale and human races. While these scenes were moving and emotional in printed form, they were mesmerizing on big screen, as the whale rider goes out to sea to converse and swim with the majestic creatures of the deep. Ihimaera has created a wonderful gift for girls all over the world in creating a girl heroine who is proactive and not crying out for boy heroes to save her. With his determination to leave this gift for his daughters, Ihimaera has created a gem in Kahu and in Nanny Flowers who encourages her every on every step of her journey.<br /><br />The writing of Witi Ihimaera reminds me of Louise Erdrich on the other side of the world. He has written countless novels, novellas, and short story collections about the Maori culture and is considered the Maori writer best known today. Part of his exposure is from the acclaim of the film version of Whale Rider, which lead many to read this gem of a book. Even though I was lead to the writing of Ihimaera in order to complete a challenge, I have a feeling that I will be reading more of his work. His writing is soothing as he talks about the special balance that Maori maintain with the earth and sea, although in my eyes I doubt any tale could top the story of a girl who can converse and swim with whales.<br /><br />5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="4183243073217544756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143011392" href="/book/show/6731023-the-whale-rider">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=read-harder-2017">read-harder-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150004676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12662446791092379355">* 2.5 *<br/><br/>I am having a wee moment of picking up New Zealand books that I should have read a long time ago and that have co-incidentally been made into films. Maurice Gee's <i> In my Fathers Den </i> was my most recent foray and off the back of that I decided to read Witi Ihimaera's novel <i> The Whale Rider </i>. Ihimaera has written quite a long list of books and short stories but <i> The Whale Rider </i> is probably his most well known due to the 2002 film of the same name. It is a beautiful film. I highly recommend</span>
  <span id="freeText12662446791092379355" style="display:none">* 2.5 *<br /><br />I am having a wee moment of picking up New Zealand books that I should have read a long time ago and that have co-incidentally been made into films. Maurice Gee's <i> In my Fathers Den </i> was my most recent foray and off the back of that I decided to read Witi Ihimaera's novel <i> The Whale Rider </i>. Ihimaera has written quite a long list of books and short stories but <i> The Whale Rider </i> is probably his most well known due to the 2002 film of the same name. It is a beautiful film. I highly recommend it. <br /><br />The book I was less enthusiastic about. What I did like was the melding of the rational world and the world of maori mythology. The opening sequence describing a primordial New Zealand complete with fairies and sentient Tuatara was quite evocative. The famous legend of Paikea who travels to NZ on the back of a whale is lovingly interpreted throughout this novel. I enjoyed Ihimaera's mythical, majestic whales right up until the point they started considering the genetic effects of oceanic radiation from Moruroa atoll, which seemed an anthropomorphism too far. <br /><br />Putting that issue to one side, in general I found the story-telling quite ham-fisted. The characters feel thin and underdeveloped. There was the odd decision to have the narrator travel to Sydney and Papua New Guinea for a few chapters. The story, in my opinion, is best when cleaving to that intersection between reality and myth. I don't think this book has aged particularly well, and might struggle against the more nuanced stories YA readers would now come to expect. <br /><br />I would love to find more NZ authors taking on our own myths and legends and weaving some fictional magic out of them but unfortunately this particular interpretation didn't work for me, but it did make an enduringly beautiful film. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12662446791092379355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1449320455" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12105174405175329305">I read this in my self-proclaimed New Zealand November, 2015. I saw the movie based on the film a few years ago but only have a vague memory of it. <br/><br/>The book comes from the perspective of Rawiri, the uncle of the girl Kahu. It is a very readable intertwining story of the modern day characters with the mythology of the gods of New Zealand and the ancient whales within their own societies and rituals. Whereas <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/133496.Once_Were_Warriors' title='Once Were Warriors by Alan Duff' rel='nofollow noopener'>Once Were Warriors</a> shows the Maori on the margins and struggling with poverty and violence</span>
  <span id="freeText12105174405175329305" style="display:none">I read this in my self-proclaimed New Zealand November, 2015. I saw the movie based on the film a few years ago but only have a vague memory of it. <br /><br />The book comes from the perspective of Rawiri, the uncle of the girl Kahu. It is a very readable intertwining story of the modern day characters with the mythology of the gods of New Zealand and the ancient whales within their own societies and rituals. Whereas <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/133496.Once_Were_Warriors" title="Once Were Warriors by Alan Duff" rel="nofollow noopener">Once Were Warriors</a> shows the Maori on the margins and struggling with poverty and violence, this novel takes a much more positive approach. The Maori in this novel are active in teaching their native languages and passing down traditions. What once was in danger of being lost - such as the ability to communicate with whales - looks like it might be preserved, if the Maori are willing to change with the times. <br /><br />Unexpectedly, there is a small diversion where the narrator travels to Australia and then to Papua New Guinea before embracing his Maori identity. This was great for me in my year of reading Oceania because he talks about the differences between the three countries and the treatment of the native populations. In particular that the PNG tribal groups had to live "one thousand year in one lifetime" because of the rate of change in technology and culture.</span>

  <span id="freeText2194372940626587974" style="display:none">A gem that glistens. Beautiful. A contemporary rewriting of an ancient Maori legend. Its messages speak of the strength of women, but even more importantly of the oneness of the past and present, the rational and the irrational, what we understand and don’t understand and of all life on earth. There is music throughout the recording, but it is the same snippet repeated over and over again. When will we get audiobooks with varied music and numerous songs?   <td colspan="2">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1871863636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1871863636" />
    <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova"><img alt="Jeannette Nikolova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480677087p2/2574284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1871863636?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeannette Nikolova" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova">Jeannette Nikolova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1871863636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13120227118035150997"><a href='https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2017/01/22/the-whale-rider-by-witi-ihimaera/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Also available on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br/><br/><b><u>Country</u>:</b> New Zealand<br/><br/>In all honesty, this was a peculiar little book. I both liked it, and didn't like it. I'm saying this in the sense that while I was reading The Whale Rider, I wasn't bored out of my mind. However, at the same time, I can't say that I actually enjoyed myself.<br/><br/><em>So in a way, this book just was. </em><br/><br/>The story was interesting in its entirety and the fairytale quality of the entire novel. There are two stories between which the narration shift</span>
  <span id="freeText13120227118035150997" style="display:none"><a href="https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2017/01/22/the-whale-rider-by-witi-ihimaera/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Also available on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br /><br /><b><u>Country</u>:</b> New Zealand<br /><br />In all honesty, this was a peculiar little book. I both liked it, and didn't like it. I'm saying this in the sense that while I was reading The Whale Rider, I wasn't bored out of my mind. However, at the same time, I can't say that I actually enjoyed myself.<br /><br /><em>So in a way, this book just was. </em><br /><br />The story was interesting in its entirety and the fairytale quality of the entire novel. There are two stories between which the narration shifts: "current times" and the birth of <em>Kahu</em>, a little girl who possesses the spirit of Maori mythology, but is not loved by her grandfather, who, as the "chief" of the community, wants a grandson and is always displeased with little Kahu; and the stories from the Maori legends about the whale riders, and the pain of a whale which was ridden by the last whale rider.<br /><br />As you can imagine, <em>Kahu's</em> story is very endearing and cute, and the whales' story has more of a surreal quality. However, this would be an oversimplification of how exactly wild this book gets at times. It's a wildness in the method and narration, rather than one in the actual events, but ultimately leads to a very fairytale-ish world of collision between myth and reality.<br /><br />This, however, can also be confusing, as I wasn't sure how I'm supposed to take the story: utter fiction? Mythological reality? Fairtytale? My confusion lead me to that awkward moment which one experiences when they meet someone who seems to be insane and one doesn't know if that person is joking/sarcastic, or really mentally unstable. (In all fairness, I'm in this situation more often than I should.)<br /><br />The other thing which a story like this heavily influences is the depth of the characters. Mythological characters are rarely very deep and well-developed, so in a book which is unsure about its allegiances with reality, expectedly, the characters were not really three intentional.<br /><br />Lastly, while I enjoyed the stories about Kahu, I was rather bored with the whale narration and the general repetitiveness of the book. Every encounter with Kahu and her grandfather, or the two of her grandparents just ended up being the exact same chapter over and over again, down to the actual expressions.<br /><br />On the positive side, I learned very interesting things, albeit minor ones, about the Maori culture and the belief system they have, to a degree. So, while this was not the most successful encounter, it was definitely not without virtues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13120227118035150997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_793243968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793243968" />
    <a title="Mmars" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2243098-mmars"><img alt="Mmars" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337885673p2/2243098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793243968?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mmars" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mmars" href="/user/show/2243098-mmars">Mmars</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793243968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10762140732611809148">Oh boy howdy I put on my ice skates and slid my way through this one. It didn't take long for me to realize that:<br/> 1) I am a jaded YA reader from years in the biz <br/>2) there's much better out there <br/>3) I would never have read this if not for my book club. <br/><br/>I really wanted to like it too. Other than the excellent <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/460635.The_Bone_People' title='The Bone People by Keri Hulme' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bone People</a> I have read little and know virtually nothing about the Maori people. Add a girl power element and mythology involving whales and I'm enticed.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, my shackles are st</span>
  <span id="freeText10762140732611809148" style="display:none">Oh boy howdy I put on my ice skates and slid my way through this one. It didn't take long for me to realize that:<br /> 1) I am a jaded YA reader from years in the biz <br />2) there's much better out there <br />3) I would never have read this if not for my book club. <br /><br />I really wanted to like it too. Other than the excellent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/460635.The_Bone_People" title="The Bone People by Keri Hulme" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bone People</a> I have read little and know virtually nothing about the Maori people. Add a girl power element and mythology involving whales and I'm enticed.<br /><br />Unfortunately, my shackles are still shaking as I think about how important it is to put well written books into children's hands in order to turn them into lifelong readers. Here's a few basics: <br />1) If you use big words, provide context <br />2) Don't dumb down<br />3) Every element of the story should clearly belong. Don't lose your reader.<br /><br />First, there were unfamiliar names in the legends. (This is excusable.) But, there were also lots of unfamiliar words in the opening scenes. Nuff said on that. I'm still struggling to decide if this book is a children's book or a YA book. At times it seemed to be written for grade schoolers and at others for young adults. Then there were things written over the heads of all of us. The narrator is sixteen years older than the subject, a young girl gifted to be the savior of her people. At times a scene would feel "childish" and at others more worldly. And only upon reflection did I understand how an "uncle" could have been killed in the car accident in New Guinea when all the Maori relatives live in New Zealand. Perhaps a very short (1-2 paragraphs) preface on terminology would have been helpful. And, when it comes right down to it, was that part of the story necessary? Would a young reader understand why it was included? <br /><br />But that's not all. I'll just dissect the scene that had me spitting spume. <br /><br />Fistfights erupt between the Maori and the New Zealanders who were mutilating beached whales. I'm going to paraphrase a bit, but here goes....<br /><br />"The gulls cried, outraged, as we vroomed through their [New Zealanders] gathering numbers. The first sight to greet out eyes was this old European lady who had sat down on a whale that some men were pulling onto the beach with a tractor. They had put a rope round the whale's rear flukes and were getting angrier and angrier with the woman, manhandling her away....We came to the rescue and that was the first fistfight of the day....."<br /><br />"There were several beefy guys loading a dismembered jaw onto the back [of a truck] As we approached we saw an old man scuffling with them. One of the young men smacked him in the mouth and the old man went down....We roared up to the truck. 'Hey, man' I hissed, 'that whale belongs to Tongaroa.'....'Who's stopping us?'...'We are," Billy said. He grabbed the chain saw [that the beefy guys were using to cut up the whales] started it up, and, next minute, had sawed the front tires of the truck. That started the second fistfight of the day. "<br /><br />Okay, I have to interject something here. Billy took the guy's chainsaw???? The beefy guy didn't like, try and stop him??? He sawed one tire and then walked/ran around the truck and then sawed the other one???? Okay, back to the story.<br /><br />"It was at this stage that the police and rangers arrived. I guess they must have had trouble figuring out who were the good guys and who were the bad guys because they started to manhandle us as well."<br /><br />Are you kidding me?????<br />So, there's a fight going on and the police/rangers don't immediately understand what's going on????<br />Good guys and bad guys???? <br />See what I mean about dumbing down????<br /><br />There's more to this scene, and it doesn't get any better.<br /><br />It's always interesting how writing reviews solidifies one's opinions of a book. I've now dropped it to one star. Just can't recommend it. I've heard the movie is really good. Skip the book. Try the movie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10762140732611809148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1476765768094191170">This is amazing - don't be put off by anyone telling you it's YA or fantasy - it isn't in my opinion. It has a child main character but I think it's YA in the same way that To Kill a Mockingbird is 'YA'. It's the sort of book you're made to read in school but you appreciate more as you get older. It's based on Maori legends, so not a 'fantasy' book but an insight into the richness that is Maori history. It also touches on the discrimination that exists between genders and races. You can learn a </span>
  <span id="freeText1476765768094191170" style="display:none">This is amazing - don't be put off by anyone telling you it's YA or fantasy - it isn't in my opinion. It has a child main character but I think it's YA in the same way that To Kill a Mockingbird is 'YA'. It's the sort of book you're made to read in school but you appreciate more as you get older. It's based on Maori legends, so not a 'fantasy' book but an insight into the richness that is Maori history. It also touches on the discrimination that exists between genders and races. You can learn a lot from this book - including how we should all respect the natural environment far more than we do. Give it a try!</span>

<div id="review_287205302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287205302" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/205963-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600122504p2/205963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287205302?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/205963-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780152050177" href="/book/show/949039.The_Whale_Rider">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/205963-lindsay?shelf=children-ya">children-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/205963-lindsay?shelf=progress-and-commentary">progress-and-commentary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/205963-lindsay?shelf=science-like">science-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/205963-lindsay?shelf=not-the-lower-48">not-the-lower-48</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/205963-lindsay?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/205963-lindsay?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287205302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4354265360062928136">Such a beautiful, challenging book. Witi Ihimaera weaves a lush story, combining land and sea, past and present. The tragic scenes were incredibly heartbreaking--between Kahu's one-sided relationship with Koro and when the whales beach themselves, I about started crying at my work desk. And the triumphs were equally brilliant--as fluid and swift as the feeling evoked as the whales sliced through the sea.<br/><br/>I would like to wonder out loud though as to the general designation of this book as children</span>
  <span id="freeText4354265360062928136" style="display:none">Such a beautiful, challenging book. Witi Ihimaera weaves a lush story, combining land and sea, past and present. The tragic scenes were incredibly heartbreaking--between Kahu's one-sided relationship with Koro and when the whales beach themselves, I about started crying at my work desk. And the triumphs were equally brilliant--as fluid and swift as the feeling evoked as the whales sliced through the sea.<br /><br />I would like to wonder out loud though as to the general designation of this book as children's literature. In the primary library in which I work, we shelve it as "J"...generally, chapter books for grade school and middle school readers. Ihimaera uses a reasonable amount of very erudite language that I imagine would be challenging even for some adult readers, and he addresses some rather adult issues of race and poaching through the novel's narrator, Kahu's Uncle Rawiri. I'm thinking specifically of two scenes: 1) The hit-and-run that occurs in Papua New Guinea when Rawiri's white friend, Jeff, hits and kills a native (and friend) on the side of the road with his family's car, and the family urges him to drive on because "It's only a native," and the tribe might seek retribution; and 2) The horrific and immensely sad scene when a herd of 200 whales beach themselves and poachers come to dismember the bodies before they've actually died.<br /><br />I wonder sometimes what differentiates a children's book from an adult book. Just because Kahu is an 8-year-old doesn't mean necessarily that it should be a book for 8-year-olds (I wouldn't suggest a child read Bastard out of Carolina just because it has a young protagonist). I think this book has definite crossover appeal along the lines of To Kill a Mockingbird, and after viewing the movie after reading this book, I can see how they toned down a lot of the various conflict in the book to make it more kid-friendly. But that's the movie, which is great in its own right, and this is the book. Other libraries consider it a Young Adult book, but in a general sense of its audience, would a teen want to read a book in which its main character only reaches the age of 8? I haven't done any research yet into this question, but I wonder if Ihimaera intended for The Whale Rider to be a children's book or if this was the publisher's marketing idea? Hmmm...just some questions.<br /><br />Despite all this(!), I really did truly enjoy the book, especially for its insight on Maori culture, the ecological concerns of a world very different from mine, and the bravery and persistence of Kahu. I would absolutely recommend it, focusing on more mature readers.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />Yay! The BBC World Book Club <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/iplayer/episode/p00mn5ln/World_Book_Club_Witi_Ihimaera_The_Whale_Rider/" rel="nofollow noopener">interviewed Witi Ihimaera</a> and used one of my questions! Ihimaera provides a moving and eye-opening commentary about the book--you should check it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4354265360062928136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_723959115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/723959115" />
    <a title="Zaid" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17345631-zaid"><img alt="Zaid" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/723959115?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zaid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zaid" href="/user/show/17345631-zaid">Zaid</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer723959115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9349915777193153034">It was an interesting book it showed how the females couldn’t gain traditional leadership of the Maori people but Kahu (short for Kahutia Te Rangi], an eight year old Maori girl who was a member of the Maori tribe of Whangara, New Zealand, kept trying to learn the ways of a leader and wants to become the chief of the tribe. Her grandfather Koro believes that this is a role reserved for males only. <br/><br/>My favourite character in this book is the main lead, Kahu. Even though she is a young eight year o</span>
  <span id="freeText9349915777193153034" style="display:none">It was an interesting book it showed how the females couldn’t gain traditional leadership of the Maori people but Kahu (short for Kahutia Te Rangi], an eight year old Maori girl who was a member of the Maori tribe of Whangara, New Zealand, kept trying to learn the ways of a leader and wants to become the chief of the tribe. Her grandfather Koro believes that this is a role reserved for males only. <br /><br />My favourite character in this book is the main lead, Kahu. Even though she is a young eight year old, she is brave, strong and determined to prove her love, her leadership and her destiny. The leader should be the first-born grandson – a direct descendant of Kahutia Te Rangi, the Whale Rider – he who rode on top of a whale from Hawaiki. However, Kahu is female and technically cannot inherit the leadership. But now there is no male heir, and the aging chief (her grandfather) is desperate to find a successor. Kahu is his only great-grandchild-and Maori tradition has no use for a girl. But when hundreds of whales beach themselves and threaten the future of the Maori tribe, it is Kahu who saves the tribe when she reveals that she has the whale rider's ancient gift of communicating with whales.<br /><br /><br />The main learning that i took from this book was that if something has been done a certain way for a certain time, it doesn't necessary need to be kept the same way. Determination and bravery goes a long way and we should do what we believe in and what we believe to be right.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book as this gave me an insight into the Maori culture but also told a story of a determined little girl and her quest to find her way into her grandfather's heart.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9349915777193153034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/670054-jess"><img alt="jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229683749p2/670054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251557188?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jess" href="/user/show/670054-jess">jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=yaf">yaf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251557188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5050551444397199189">This book alternated between ancient mythology and the modern struggle of a young girl trying to take her place in society. The mythology portions tell the story of the whale rider, who was a long-ago ancestor who rode a giant ancient whale to the land where the Maori tribe of Whangara, New Zealand live. The young girl is Eight-year-old Kahu. Kahu is the only great-grandchild of an aging chief who is desperate for a male heir to take his title. <br/><br/>So, the parts about the mythology and the internal </span>
  <span id="freeText5050551444397199189" style="display:none">This book alternated between ancient mythology and the modern struggle of a young girl trying to take her place in society. The mythology portions tell the story of the whale rider, who was a long-ago ancestor who rode a giant ancient whale to the land where the Maori tribe of Whangara, New Zealand live. The young girl is Eight-year-old Kahu. Kahu is the only great-grandchild of an aging chief who is desperate for a male heir to take his title. <br /><br />So, the parts about the mythology and the internal narrative of the giant whale were not the most compelling passages to me, but I liked Kahu and her struggle to be accepted by her grandfather. Her persistent love and optimism shone brightly through the old chief's scowl. You have to suspend disbelief almost entirely to get through the plot, but I enjoyed the journey. <br /><br />Note: there is a scene where a lot of giant whales start beaching themselves near Whangara. I know it's like, a metaphor for everything that's wrong but it made me so sad. I was seriously emotional. I would love to forget it, but it won't get out of my brain. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5050551444397199189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1440788620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1440788620" />
    <a title="Michelle Boyer-Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly"><img alt="Michelle Boyer-Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568748753p2/48727895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1440788620?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Boyer-Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Boyer-Kelly" href="/user/show/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly">Michelle Boyer-Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=indigenous-feminism">indigenous-feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=ph-d-books">ph-d-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=adaptation-lit">adaptation-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=oral-tradition">oral-tradition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=gender-studies">gender-studies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=indigenous-studies">indigenous-studies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=maori-studies">maori-studies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727895-michelle-boyer-kelly?shelf=motherhood">motherhood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1440788620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2421713942904201993">Witi Ihimaera wrote the novel <i>Whale Rider</i> in response to his daughter’s wondering why there were no female heroes in the stories and films they were viewing—such a wonderful question for 1987 when most literature did revolve, arguably, around male characters—but even more significantly, Ihimaera’s daughters also expressed concern that there were even fewer Maori characters in the world. Thus, the novel (later to become a film adaptation) was born. It is a great example of Maori literature, Young</span>
  <span id="freeText2421713942904201993" style="display:none">Witi Ihimaera wrote the novel <i>Whale Rider</i> in response to his daughter’s wondering why there were no female heroes in the stories and films they were viewing—such a wonderful question for 1987 when most literature did revolve, arguably, around male characters—but even more significantly, Ihimaera’s daughters also expressed concern that there were even fewer Maori characters in the world. Thus, the novel (later to become a film adaptation) was born. It is a great example of Maori literature, Young Adult Literature, and so much more. I have included some highlights below, broken down by section. <br /><br /><b>Prologue</b><br />-	“The only reluctant ones were the fairy people, who retreated with their silver laughter to caves in glistening waterfalls” (p5)<br />-	“For the sacred sign was on the monster, a swirling tattoo imprinted on the forehead” (p5)<br />-	“And the song in the sea drenched the air with ageless music, and land and sea opened themselves to him, the gift long waited for: <i>tangata</i>, man” (p6)<br />-	“It flew across a thousand years” (p6)<br />-	“Let it be done” (p7) –a phrase that is repeated as part of oral tradition<br /><br /><b>Spring</b><br />-	Birthing of the whale (p11)<br />-	“Watching, the ancient bull whale was swept up in memories of his own birthing. His mother had been saved by sharks three months later; crying over her in the shallows of Hawaiki, he had been succored by the golden human who became his master” (p11)<br />-	“But his elder females were fearful; for them, that rhapsody of adolescence, that song of the flute, seemed only to signify that their leader was turning his thoughts to the dangerous islands to the southwest” (p12)<br />-	Grandfather Koro upset that the first daughter of the family is a girl, stating “She has broken the male line of descent in our tribe” (p13)<br />-	“Koro Apirana could not reconcile his traditional beliefs about Maori leadership and rights with Kahu’s birth. By Maori custom, leadership was hereditary, and normally the mantle of prestige fell from the eldest son to the eldest son. Except that in this case, there was an eldest daughter” (p16)<br />-	Traditional burial of the birth cord is discussed (p20-21)<br />-	Whales call from the sea, saying “Let it be done” (p23)<br /><br /><b>Summer</b><br />-	The section is subtitled Halcyon’s Flight; can be used as an adjective to be idyllic, peaceful time; in literature an Asian/African kingfisher; as a noun is a mythical bird who breeds in a floating nest at sea at the winter solstice, charming the wind and the waves into a calm (p25)<br />-	“The elderly females assisted the younger mothers, shepherding the newborn in the first journey from the cetacean crib” (p27)<br />-	Rehua, Kahu’s mother, dies (p29)<br />-	“It was surprising how closely Kahu and Koro Apirana resembled each other. The only difference was that she loved him but he didn’t love her” (p33-34)<br />-	The purpose of new instructions are “to keep the Maori language going, and to increase the strength of the tribe” (p35)<br />-	“Whenever asked, the whale would attend the call, as long as the mariner possessed the necessary authority and knew the way of talking to whales” (p40)<br />-	“… some people say the whale was transformed into an island” (p40)<br />-	“So it was that ceremonials of respect were employed between man and sea. For instance, finish was sacred and women therefore did not go out with the men, and fishing grounds became steeped in special rituals to ensure their bounty” (p41)<br />-	“…in these days of commercialism, it is not always easy to resist temptation” (p50)<br />-	“Listen to how empty our sea has become” (p50)<br /><br /><b>Autumn</b><br />-	Paikea the sea god is first mentioned (p57); keep in mind that in the film adaptation Kuha is actually named Pai<br />-	“Koro had accepted that Porourangi would be ‘the one’ in our generation to carry on the leadership of the people, but he was still looking for ‘the one’ in the next generation” (p71)<br />-	“Our Koro was like an old whale stranded in an alien present, but that was how it was supposed to be, because he also had his role in the pattern of things, in the tides of the future” (p72)<br />-	“… I loved her all the more for her vulnerability” (p86)<br />-	“…young girl who was not really so brave and who would have liked the support of the one person who was never there—her Koro” (p87) in regards to the fact that Koro misses an important school event that Kahu invited him to<br /><br /><b>Winter</b><br />-	“But the whales were like confused children, milling and jostling out in the deeper water, and they kept trying to return to those who were still stranded along the beach, darting back to those who were already dead” (p105)<br />-	“I will never forget the look on Kahu’s face. She was gazing out to sea and it was as if she was looking back into the past. It was a look of calm, of acceptance. It forced s all to turn to see what Kahu was seeing” (p111) <br />-	“On the head of the whale was the sacred sign. A swirling tattoo, flashing its power across the darkening sky” (p113)<br />-	There is a whale rider<br />-	“… it is time for the women to act the men” (p121)<br />-	“There is no place for it here in this world. The people who once commanded it are no longer here … When it dies, we die. I die” says Koro when discussing the whale washed up (p122)<br />-	“The tribe watched in silence, waiting for the whale to die” (p123)<br /><br /><b>Epilogue</b><br />-	“The sea hissed and sparkled with love for the ancient bull whale, and every now and then, the oldest mother whale would close in on him, gently, to nuzzle him, caress him, and kiss him just to let him know how much he had been missed. But in her heart of hearts, she knew that he was badly wounded and near to exhaustion” (p137)<br />-	Discussion of a “sign of feminine submission” (p140)<br />-	“She wanted to make sure that the bull whale really understood that the rider was Paikea’s descendant, and if it was not returned to the surface and taken back to the land, then it would not fulfill its tasks” (p141)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2421713942904201993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1214679031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1214679031" />
    <a title="Shakaela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25811652-shakaela"><img alt="Shakaela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413598640p2/25811652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1214679031?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shakaela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shakaela" href="/user/show/25811652-shakaela">Shakaela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1214679031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8885128520597131085">"The Whale Rider" was a book I was quite drawn to, as I am a kiwi, and I love New Zealand. I really felt for Kahu (or Pai) especially, and now I will look up to her as a favoured character. If I was in English class, I'd write a long descript essay into the characters and the morals etc... But I don't feel the need for that level of depth right now. <br/><br/>I really liked being carried back to the days before I was born in Aotearoa, and then feeling the effects history has on a country and its people. I</span>
  <span id="freeText8885128520597131085" style="display:none">"The Whale Rider" was a book I was quite drawn to, as I am a kiwi, and I love New Zealand. I really felt for Kahu (or Pai) especially, and now I will look up to her as a favoured character. If I was in English class, I'd write a long descript essay into the characters and the morals etc... But I don't feel the need for that level of depth right now. <br /><br />I really liked being carried back to the days before I was born in Aotearoa, and then feeling the effects history has on a country and its people. It was interesting how the folklore of Pai weaved into Kahu's family, although I take the stories lightly as I have faith only in the one true God.<br /><br />I'm in the process of learning the Maori language, so I liked how Maori words were incorporated into the book, as I had the chance to catch onto some new words.<br /><br />If you read this book, you will have a greater love and understanding for culture and diversity, and hopefully appreciate your brothers and sisters more if you haven't before. I want to watch the movie now. :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="8885128520597131085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1802513439" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1802513439" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6505203-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439308300p2/6505203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1802513439?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/6505203-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6505203-wendy?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6505203-wendy?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802513439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7543090848993790259">This is a super fast read, unsurprisingly, given the reading level. There are a lot of Maori words--don't make my mistake and find out about the glossary halfway through the book, yeah? It's back there, and very useful.<br/><br/>The story is good, if a little...oddly told. The choice to render the story from the uncle's point of view was odd and annoyed me a few times. That said, it has some very beautiful parts in it, and I think it's a good book to have kids read.<br/><br/>This is going to sound like sacrilege, b</span>
  <span id="freeText7543090848993790259" style="display:none">This is a super fast read, unsurprisingly, given the reading level. There are a lot of Maori words--don't make my mistake and find out about the glossary halfway through the book, yeah? It's back there, and very useful.<br /><br />The story is good, if a little...oddly told. The choice to render the story from the uncle's point of view was odd and annoyed me a few times. That said, it has some very beautiful parts in it, and I think it's a good book to have kids read.<br /><br />This is going to sound like sacrilege, but...in this case, I liked the movie better--I would give the movie all five stars, if I were rating it here. It's probably because I saw it before I read it, and also because I'm not a kid, so for me the story went a little <i>too</i> fast and skated right over things that, in a book for adults, might have meant some meaty drama. The movie wasn't for kids, so it doesn't have that problem.<br /><br />Still, it will only take you a couple of hours, maybe less, and you won't regret having read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7543090848993790259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="eRin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1090413-erin"><img alt="eRin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427907838p2/1090413.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20457977?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="eRin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="eRin" href="/user/show/1090413-erin">eRin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1090413-erin?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1090413-erin?shelf=grown-up-books">grown-up-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20457977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2914547726710893501">Kahu is the eldest great-grandchild of Kori, the chief of the Maori in Whangara, New Zealand. Unfortunately, Kahu is a girl and therefore Kori has no interest in her because he is only focused on finding the next leader of the tribe. Kahu showers Kori with love and admiration despite the fact that he continuously dismisses her and he continues his classes for the the males in the tribe and searches for the "one." <br/><br/>This is a heartwarming story of a detrmined little girl and her quest to find her w</span>
  <span id="freeText2914547726710893501" style="display:none">Kahu is the eldest great-grandchild of Kori, the chief of the Maori in Whangara, New Zealand. Unfortunately, Kahu is a girl and therefore Kori has no interest in her because he is only focused on finding the next leader of the tribe. Kahu showers Kori with love and admiration despite the fact that he continuously dismisses her and he continues his classes for the the males in the tribe and searches for the "one." <br /><br />This is a heartwarming story of a detrmined little girl and her quest to find her way into her great-grandfather's heart. The combination of Maori legend and the present day is amazing and makes for an interesting and good novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2914547726710893501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2973239445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3406520229896827789"><b>
  <i>Set text for University</i>
</b><br/><br/>A short rewriting of an ancient Maori legend juxtaposed with the present day. I enjoyed the insight into primordial New Zealand and their culture rich with fairy tales. Young Kahu has the misfortune of not being born the boy her Great-Grandfather, Koro, so desperately wanted and her one-sided relationship with him was heart-breaking. Yet, despite her age, she possessed an admirable determination to prove her love and her destiny. <br/><br/>Although the unfamiliar vocabulary stif</span>
  <span id="freeText3406520229896827789" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Set text for University</i>
</b><br /><br />A short rewriting of an ancient Maori legend juxtaposed with the present day. I enjoyed the insight into primordial New Zealand and their culture rich with fairy tales. Young Kahu has the misfortune of not being born the boy her Great-Grandfather, Koro, so desperately wanted and her one-sided relationship with him was heart-breaking. Yet, despite her age, she possessed an admirable determination to prove her love and her destiny. <br /><br />Although the unfamiliar vocabulary stifled my reading at times, The Whale Rider is a poignant exploration of gender politics and coming of age in a changing world.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3406520229896827789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_223663366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223663366" />
    <a title="Judy Croome" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4240599-judy-croome"><img alt="Judy Croome" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584884676p2/4240599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223663366?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy Croome" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy Croome" href="/user/show/4240599-judy-croome">Judy Croome</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780152050177" href="/book/show/949039.The_Whale_Rider">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223663366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7656582170297417411">Written in 1987, THE WHALE RIDER is a deceptively short book. Only 120 pages long, it’s a richly layered story dealing with several major social issues: family relationships, gender discrimination, generational differences, racial prejudice, loss of the cultural identity of indigenous tribes, ecological conservationism and modern man’s disconnection from his spiritual self.<br/><br/>Kahu is a young Maori girl who, from the moment of her birth, had a deep connection with her great-grandfather Koro Apirana,</span>
  <span id="freeText7656582170297417411" style="display:none">Written in 1987, THE WHALE RIDER is a deceptively short book. Only 120 pages long, it’s a richly layered story dealing with several major social issues: family relationships, gender discrimination, generational differences, racial prejudice, loss of the cultural identity of indigenous tribes, ecological conservationism and modern man’s disconnection from his spiritual self.<br /><br />Kahu is a young Maori girl who, from the moment of her birth, had a deep connection with her great-grandfather Koro Apirana, a powerful Maori Chieftan. Custodian of his people’s indigenous culture, Koro searches desperately for his successor: a boy who, for the good of all his people, will value and understand the ancient Maori traditions as much as Koro does. Kahu’s uncle Rawiri, who narrates most of the story, and her great-grandmother Nanni Flowers, see in Kahu’s spirit that which Koro seeks: the soul of the future Chieftan who will lead the Maoris of Whangara into the 21st century. But Kahu is a girl and, in Maori tradition, only men can perform the sacred traditions that keep the Maori people blessed of their gods and their ancestors.<br /><br />From the delightfully subversive feminist Nanni Flowers to good guy Rawiri who, along with a diverse group of people tried desperately to save 200 beached whales (one of the several scenes in the book which had me sobbing out loud), to the serene, compassionate and otherworldly Kahu, the story is filled with remarkable characters. These include the Old Whale, an ancient sea-creature that has survived for centuries to ensure that Kahu meets her destiny of ensuring that the sacred Maori traditions shall live on into the new century.<br /><br />The lyrical, almost magical, descriptions of the herd of whales’ journeys through the depths of the great oceans contrast beautifully with Rawiri’s simple, down-to-earth narrative. The boneless, weightless feel of the writing in the whale scenes recreate both a transcendent spiritual state and the sensation of swimming underwater. From the comical rendition of the constant bickering of Koro Apirana and his wife Nanni Flowers, to the well of emotion that has him spontaneously performing the haka to support Kahu at her school prize-giving, Rawiri’s gentle perceptions of his extended Maori family reveal the deep bonds of love and culture holding them together. “Family,” he says to his white friend Jeff, “is Family.” <br /><br />Some of the Maori terms were, at times, confusing and the edition I read did not have a glossary of Maori terms, which would have been useful. <br /> <br />This lack, however, did not detract from the lush splendour of THE WHALE RIDER, a beautiful story of hope and promise. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7656582170297417411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2249392644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2249392644" />
    <a title="Sue K H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4047077-sue-k-h"><img alt="Sue K H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544723126p2/4047077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2249392644?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue K H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue K H" href="/user/show/4047077-sue-k-h">Sue K H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2249392644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8324245999576471397">I adored the film The Whale Rider and didn't know it was adapted from a book until I saw it on Goodreads. I had to read it, especially since it fits in one of my challenges. The Author, Witi Ihimaera, wrote this story after his daughters complained that all the heroes in movies were men and the women were always helpless.<br/><br/>Ihimaera's response was a beautifully crafted heartwarming story about fictional aboriginal people in NewZeland in the Maori tribe. The Maori tribal leader, Karo, is upset when </span>
  <span id="freeText8324245999576471397" style="display:none">I adored the film The Whale Rider and didn't know it was adapted from a book until I saw it on Goodreads. I had to read it, especially since it fits in one of my challenges. The Author, Witi Ihimaera, wrote this story after his daughters complained that all the heroes in movies were men and the women were always helpless.<br /><br />Ihimaera's response was a beautifully crafted heartwarming story about fictional aboriginal people in NewZeland in the Maori tribe. The Maori tribal leader, Karo, is upset when the great grandson he hopes for turns out to be a girl who they name Kahu. Kahu's father is to succeed Karo as the leader when he passes, and his first born child is then supposed to succeed him in following their custom. Karo is crushed by the fact that he will have to find another successor because a woman is not suitable to be chief in his eyes. He is so upset that he shuns his great granddaughter. Despite her grandfather not wanting anything to do with her, Kuha spends her life trying to win him over. She grows up believing that she is capable of being Chief some day without any encouragement. <br /><br />It's a heart wrenching story that's great for young girls especially. I hate to say it, but I liked the movie more. It was a five star film for me. I teared up multiple times in the theater. The book didn't have the same power for me, but there's a reason it inspired such a great film. It's a great story that's definitely worth reading. 4 Stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8324245999576471397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1033913425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1033913425" />
    <a title="Elizabeth A" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3123067-elizabeth-a"><img alt="Elizabeth A" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420475630p2/3123067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1033913425?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth A" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth A" href="/user/show/3123067-elizabeth-a">Elizabeth A</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781743110829" href="/book/show/13352306-whale-rider-the">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3123067-elizabeth-a?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3123067-elizabeth-a?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1033913425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer637014974379853431">I saw the movie based on this novella when it came out years ago, and remember really liking it. I listened to the audiobook wonderfully narrated by Jay Laga'aia, and would recommend the audio as there are Maori phrases and music that add to the enjoyment of this story. <br/><br/>I love creation stories, and this one retells an ancient Maori legend juxtaposed with the present day lives of the Maori. Kahu is a young Maori girl who has the misfortune of not being born the boy her Great-Grandfather desperate</span>
  <span id="freeText637014974379853431" style="display:none">I saw the movie based on this novella when it came out years ago, and remember really liking it. I listened to the audiobook wonderfully narrated by Jay Laga'aia, and would recommend the audio as there are Maori phrases and music that add to the enjoyment of this story. <br /><br />I love creation stories, and this one retells an ancient Maori legend juxtaposed with the present day lives of the Maori. Kahu is a young Maori girl who has the misfortune of not being born the boy her Great-Grandfather desperately wanted. This story switches back and forth between her struggle to find her place in the world, and the reminiscences of the ancient whale of legends. The book is populated with wonderful characters, and explores themes of holding on to one's culture in a modern world, gender politics, and coming of age in a changing world. While written for a young adult audience, this one is a lovely read for adults as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="637014974379853431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NMSHr+FHzEQtItWKJt3n6ImgBlkOps+4gZqrfC/7aF2BYLuZLrTqLI8R4Uy9A+SpJn7teHB1jV1YQ9WMJzL3ug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4zfN22jXLmigLXfN72ALRMLbv3t/ca+H3rDY+Yz+HnNWk/HtpyQIAAIeQwt0vggFbQVUWgGi7WIHaaYJhDeBlA==')})
  }
